<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#CCF; font-weight:bold"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikipe-tan_face.svg"><img alt="Wikipe-tan face.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="440" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/16px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/24px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wikipe-tan_face.svg/32px-Wikipe-tan_face.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portal:Anime_and_Manga" title="Portal:Anime and Manga">Anime and Manga portal</a></td>

<p><i><b>Rozen Maiden</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ローゼンメイデン</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <i>Rōzen Meiden</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> series written and illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Peach-Pit" title="Peach-Pit">Peach-Pit</a>. It was serialized in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monthly_Comic_Birz" title="Monthly Comic Birz">Monthly Comic Birz</a></i> between the September 2002 and July 2007 issues. The individual chapters were collected and released into eight <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes by <a href="/wiki/Gentosha" title="Gentosha">Gentosha</a>. The eight volumes were localized to North America by <a href="/wiki/Tokyopop" title="Tokyopop">Tokyopop</a> between March 2003 and June 2007. The story follows Jun Sakurada, a middle school student who withdrew from society after suffering persecutions from his classmates. Following his withdrawal, he is chosen to become the master to a Rozen Maiden named Shinku. Rozen Maidens are seven sentient <a href="/wiki/Bisque_doll" title="Bisque doll">bisque dolls</a> who compete against each other to become a perfect doll dubbed as Alice.</p>
<p><i>Rozen Maiden</i> received a sequel under the series' <a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">katakana</a> title. It was serialized in <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Young_Jump" title="Weekly Young Jump">Weekly Young Jump</a></i> between April 2008 and January 2014. <i>Rozen Maiden</i> has spun off anthology manga and novel stories, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_book" title="Art book">art books</a>, and four <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> series; the four anime series are titled <i>Rozen Maiden</i>, <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i>, <i>Rozen Maiden: Ouvertüre</i>, and <i>Rozen Maiden: Zurückspulen</i>. <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">Tokyo Broadcasting System</a> were the producers for the anime with <a href="/wiki/Nomad_(company)" title="Nomad (company)">Nomad</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Animation_studio" title="Animation studio">animation studio</a> for the first three series and <a href="/wiki/Studio_Deen" title="Studio Deen">Studio Deen</a> for <i>Zurückspulen</i>. The anime adaptions resulted in several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rozen_Maiden_discography" title="Rozen Maiden discography">audio disc releases</a> and three video games.</p>
<p>In 2007, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneon_Universal_Entertainment" title="Geneon Universal Entertainment">Geneon Entertainment USA</a> licensed the first two anime series for North American release and had later signed <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation</a> on as a distributor, after shutting down in September 2007. In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Sentai_Filmworks" title="Sentai Filmworks">Sentai Filmworks</a> acquired both seasons as well as the third series; they made the three series available for streaming on <a href="/wiki/Anime_Network" title="Anime Network">Anime Network</a>. <a href="/wiki/Crunchyroll" title="Crunchyroll">Crunchyroll</a> later acquired streaming rights to the first two series. For the fourth series, Sentai Filmworks had acquired the license for digital and home video release, while Crunchyroll acquired streaming rights.</p>
<p>Tokyopop's volumes of <i>Rozen Maiden</i> have appeared on ICv2's monthly top one-hundred selling graphic novels. Reviews towards the manga were generally positive with reviewers praising balance in drama and comedy. For the anime, reception towards the first series was mixed while <i>Träumend</i> was mostly negative.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Rozen_Maiden_characters" title="List of Rozen Maiden characters">List of Rozen Maiden characters</a></div>
<p>In the 20th century, a legendary doll maker named Rozen created seven <a href="/wiki/Bisque_doll" title="Bisque doll">bisque dolls</a> which were powered and given sentience with a gem called Rosa Mystica.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 2</a></sup> Since then, Rozen sent the dolls away to find masters and to battle among themselves to gather each other's Rosa Mysticas; this competition is referred to as the Alice Game. When a doll obtains all seven, they are to become a perfect doll dubbed as Alice and will be reunited with Rozen.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 5</a></sup> By order of creation, the seven Rozen Maidens are named <a href="#Suigintou">Suigintou</a>, <a href="#Kanaria">Kanaria</a>, <a href="#Suiseiseki">Suiseiseki</a>, <a href="#Souseiseki">Souseiseki</a>, <a href="#Shinku">Shinku</a>, <a href="#Hinaichigo">Hinaichigo</a>, and <a href="#Kirakisho">Kirakisho</a>.</p>
<p><i>Rozen Maiden</i> follows Jun Sakurada, a middle school student who has withdrawn from society after suffering persecutions from his classmates. He is chosen to become Shinku's master and joins the Alice Game.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Prologue 2</a></sup> As the series progresses, Jun also becomes the master to Hinaichigo and Suiseiseki. After Souseiseki's Rosa Mystica is taken by Suigintou, Jun's Rozen Maidens resolve to revive her and to end the Alice Game peacefully;<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 21</a></sup> they later befriend Kanaria who shares their sentiments. However, the group is attacked by Kirakisho who absorbs Hinaichigo and traps Shinku and Suiseiseki in the N-field, a <a href="/wiki/Plane_(esotericism)" title="Plane (esotericism)">plane</a> of consciousness which connects the universe. <i>Rozen Maiden</i> concludes with Jun preparing to enter the N-field to save the dolls.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 43</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Rozen Maiden</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s plot is continued in the sequel serialization which uses the katakana title of the series.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_KK"><a href="#endnote_KK">KK</a></sup> Inside the N-field, Jun is forced into hiding by Kirakisho and contacts an adult version of himself from an alternate world.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 1</a></sup> The adult Jun is able to free Shinku and unite the Rozen Maidens to defeat Kirakisho.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 25</a></sup> Kirakisho returns and successfully captures all the Rozen Maidens' masters. The Rozen Maidens pursue her eventually resulting in most of their defeat except Shinku and Kirakisho. Shinku's sympathy towards Kirakisho's loneliness convinces the latter to surrender her Rosa Mystica. With all seven gathered, Shinku becomes Alice.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 65</a></sup> Using her new powers, Shinku revives her sisters and is put into a coma in return.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 66</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt><span id="Jun_Sakurada">Jun Sakurada</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">桜田 ジュン</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Sakurada Jun</i>)</span></dt>
<dd>Jun is a middle school student who withdrew from society after he was outed and bullied for being a dress designer.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 27</a></sup> Since then, he becomes irritated whenever something related to school is brought up and sinks into a depression when pressured on the topic. His interactions with the Rozen Maidens and their masters changes his outlook on life and he works up the courage to return to society. He has an older sister named Nori Sakurada<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[Jp 1]</a></sup>. Jun is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Asami_Sanada" title="Asami Sanada">Asami Sanada</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Mona_Marshall" title="Mona Marshall">Mona Marshall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></dd>
<dd>In an alternate world without Rozen Maidens, Jun eventually returns to society and is a friendless university student who works at a bookstore.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 1</a></sup> His interactions with Shinku gives him the opportunity to befriend his co-worker, Saitou<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[Jp 2]</a></sup>, which leads him to join a theatrics club. At the end of the series, he becomes Kirakisho's master.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 66</a></sup> The adult Jun is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Ry%C5%8Dta_%C5%8Csaka" title="Ryōta Ōsaka">Ryōta Ōsaka</a> in Japanese,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff-5">[3]</a></sup> and Corey Hartzog in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[4]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><span id="Rozen_Maidens">Rozen Maidens</span></dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rozen_Maiden_drama_2013.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="300" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Rozen_Maiden_drama_2013.png/220px-Rozen_Maiden_drama_2013.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/93/Rozen_Maiden_drama_2013.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rozen_Maiden_drama_2013.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Rozen Maidens with Shinku in the center. From top going clockwise: Suigintou, Kanaria, Suiseiseki, Souseiseki, Hinaichigo, Kirakisho.</div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dd>A legendary doll maker named Rozen <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ローゼン</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rōzen</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> wanted to create a perfect doll dubbed as Alice. His attempts resulted in seven sentient bisque dolls which became known as Rozen Maidens.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 13</a></sup> The dolls' sentient nature are powered by a magical gem called Rosa Mystica. To become Alice, a Rozen Maiden must gather all seven Rosa Mysticas; this contest is referred to as the Alice Game. Each Rozen Maiden has a production order, their own personal suitcase, and are accompanied by an artificial spirit which serves the doll. Rozen Maidens rely on a contract with a human master to supply themselves with power for battle.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 6</a></sup> Since then, Rozen has forgo a physical body and lives within the N-field, waiting for Alice.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 62</a></sup>
<ul>
<li><span id="Suigintou">Suigintou</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">水銀燈</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Suigintō</i>)</span> is the first Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Meimei<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[Jp 3]</a></sup>. She is the most ambitious of her sisters and wishes to become Alice to earn Rozen's love.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 29</a></sup> Suigintou possesses black wings which she uses for mobility and offensive purposes. Her master is Megu Kakizaki<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[Jp 4]</a></sup>, an ill girl with a cynical personality.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 23</a></sup> Megu sees Suigintou as an angel of death who will end her suffering. Suigintou is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Rie_Tanaka" title="Rie Tanaka">Rie Tanaka</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Karen_Strassman" title="Karen Strassman">Karen Strassman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup> Megu is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Shiho_Kawaragi" title="Shiho Kawaragi">Shiho Kawaragi</a> and English dubbed by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Erika_Weinstein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Erika Weinstein (page does not exist)">Erika Weinstein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Kanaria">Kanaria</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">金糸雀</span>)</span> is the second Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Pizzicato<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[Jp 5]</a></sup>. She is sociable, energetic, eccentric and habitually ends her sentences with lit. "Possibly" <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">かしら〜</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kashira</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>. She was initially a loyal participant of the Alice game but is convinced for a peaceful lifestyle instead. For battle, she plays her violin and manipulates the sound waves to cause destruction. Her master is Mitsu Kusabue<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[Jp 6]</a></sup>, a doll clothing designer. Mitsu greatly adores the Rozen Maidens which scares the dolls. Kanaria is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Yumi_Shimura" title="Yumi Shimura">Yumi Shimura</a> and English dubbed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cristina_Valenzuela" title="Cristina Valenzuela">Cristina Valenzuela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup> Mitsu is voiced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akiko_Kawase_(actor)" title="Akiko Kawase (actor)">Akiko Kawase</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Philece_Sampler" title="Philece Sampler">Philece Sampler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Suiseiseki">Suiseiseki</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">翠星石</span>)</span> is the third Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Sui Dream<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[Jp 7]</a></sup>. She is a <a href="/wiki/Tsundere" title="Tsundere">tsundere</a>; she openly insults others but does care about them. Suiseiseki speaks with the copula <a href="/wiki/Copula_(linguistics)#Japanese" title="Copula (linguistics)">desu</a> and always speaks in third person. She has no intention of participating in the Alice Game and only wishes to live happily with her twin sister, Souseiseki.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 25</a></sup> Suiseiseki's ability is to supply nourishment to souls and memories and is able to summon plants for offensive purposes with her watering can.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 19</a></sup> Jun becomes her master during the events of the series.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 17</a></sup> Suiseiseki is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Natsuko_Kuwatani" title="Natsuko Kuwatani">Natsuko Kuwatani</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Forstadt" title="Rebecca Forstadt">Rebecca Forstadt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Souseiseki">Souseiseki</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">蒼星石</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Sōseiseki</i>)</span> is the fourth Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Lempicka<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[Jp 8]</a></sup>. She speaks in as masculine manner and has a strong sense of duty towards her master and role as a Rozen Maiden. Souseiseki's ability is to cut souls and memories with her scissors.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 19</a></sup> Her master is Kazuha Yuibishi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[Jp 9]</a></sup>, a rich man who is haunted by his twin brother's death. Kazuha disproved of his brother's marriage forcing the latter elope and drown in a ferry accident; as such, he intends to use Souseiseki to make his brother's widow suffer. After Souseiseki reveals Kazuha's hatred comes from grief she uses her abilities to leave him at peace.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 20</a></sup> During the series, Souseiseki's Rosa Mystica is taken by Suigintou and her body by Kirakisho. Souseiseki is later, revived and becomes Jun's Rozen Maiden.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 16</a></sup> Afterwards, Souseiseki willingly gives Suigintou her Rosa Mystica.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 50</a></sup> Souseiseki is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Rika_Morinaga" title="Rika Morinaga">Rika Morinaga</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Julie_Ann_Taylor" title="Julie Ann Taylor">Julie Ann Taylor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup> In the anime series by Nomad, Souseiseki's master is an elderly man who substitutes her for his dead son though he overcomes his grief afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ep_9_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ep_9-14">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Shinku">Shinku</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">真紅</span>)</span> is the fifth Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Hollie<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[Jp 10]</a></sup>. She has a <a href="/wiki/Southern_belle" title="Southern belle">southern belle</a> personality and treats Jun as her servant. Shinku treats regular dolls as if they are alive, and is an avid fan of the fictional puppet show Detective Kun Kun<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[Jp 11]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 14</a></sup> Shinku wishes to complete the Alice Game without killing her siblings.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 6</a></sup> For battles, she is able to create and control rose petals. She is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Miyuki_Sawashiro" title="Miyuki Sawashiro">Miyuki Sawashiro</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Mela_Lee" title="Mela Lee">Mela Lee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Hinaichigo">Hinaichigo</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">雛苺</span>)</span> is the sixth Rozen Maiden and is accompanied by the artificial spirit Berrybell<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[Jp 12]</a></sup>. She has a childlike personality and dislikes being alone.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 30</a></sup> She often ends her sentences with "na no" <span style="font-weight:normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">なの〜</span><span class="t_nihongo_help"><sup><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span style="color:#00e; font:bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration:none; padding:0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup></span>)</span> and occasionally speaks in French. For battle, Hinaichigo is able to summon and control strawberry vines.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 8</a></sup> Her master was Tomoe Kashiwaba<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[Jp 13]</a></sup>, Jun's classmate who delivers his school work during his withdrawal. When Hinaichigo's naivety endangers Tomoe's life, Shinku defeats Hinaichigo in the Alice Game and has her become a servant instead of taking her Rosa Mystica.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 6</a></sup> During the series, Hinaichigo is absorbed by Kirakisho and gives her Rosa Mystica to Shinku.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 35</a></sup> Hinaichigo is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Sakura_Nogawa" title="Sakura Nogawa">Sakura Nogawa</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Sherry_Lynn" title="Sherry Lynn">Sherry Lynn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup> Tomoe is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Masayo_Kurata" title="Masayo Kurata">Masayo Kurata</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Elias-Fahn" title="Dorothy Elias-Fahn">Dorothy Elias-Fahn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-9"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><span id="Kirakisho">Kirakisho</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">雪華綺晶</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Kirakishō</i>)</span> is the seventh Rozen Maiden who is accompanied by the artificial spirit Rosary<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[Jp 14]</a></sup>. She was created without a physical body as Rozen tested whether physical limitations prevented him from creating Alice.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 34</a></sup> Her ability allows her to materialize illusions. Because she can not exist outside the N-Field, her main goal is to capture the Rozen Maiden's masters to ease her loneliness. After her defeat, Kirakisho uses her illusions to create a middle school student named Kaito Toriumi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[Jp 15]</a></sup> to replace Rozen and to craft imitated Rozen Maidens to be her sister. Following her second defeat, Kirakisho is touched by Shinku's love and surrenders her Rosa Mystica.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 65</a></sup> She was later revived with a physical body and is in possession of the adult Jun.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Tale"><a href="#endnote_Tale">Tale 66</a></sup> Kirakisho is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Chiemi_Chiba" title="Chiemi Chiba">Chiemi Chiba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff-5">[3]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><span id="Laplace.27s_Demon">Laplace's Demon</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ラプラスの魔</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rapurasu no Ma</i>)</span></dt>
<dd>Laplace's Demon is a humanoid with a rabbit's head who dwells in the N-field.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Phase"><a href="#endnote_Phase">Phase 5</a></sup> He is the referee to the Alice Game and often assists the protagonists through riddles or as a directional guide. He is voiced in <i>Träumend</i> and <i>Ouvertüre</i> by <a href="/wiki/Kyousei_Tsukui" title="Kyousei Tsukui">Kyousei Tsukui</a> with English dubbing by <a href="/wiki/Keith_Silverstein" title="Keith Silverstein">Keith Silverstein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laplace_voice_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laplace_voice-21">[6]</a></sup> In <i>Zurückspulen</i>, he is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Mikami" title="Satoshi Mikami">Satoshi Mikami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laplace_voice_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Laplace_voice-21">[6]</a></sup></dd>
<dt><span id="Bara-Suishou">Bara-Suishou</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">薔薇水晶</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Barasuishō</i>)</span> and <span id="Enju">Enju</span> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">槐</span>)</span></dt>
<dd>Bara-Suishou and Enju are characters who appear in the <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> anime and audio drama. Enju is Rozen's apprentice and the creator of Bara-Suishou, an imitation of a Rozen Maiden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TEp_12_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-TEp_12-22">[7]</a></sup> Enju plots a battle between Bara-Suishou and the Rozen Maidens in order to prove his superiority over Rozen. Once Bara-Suishou gathered six Rosa Mysticas, her body overloads, killing her and Enju.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TEp_12_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-TEp_12-22">[7]</a></sup> Bara-Suishou is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Saori_Got%C5%8D" title="Saori Gotō">Saori Gotō</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Tara_Platt" title="Tara Platt">Tara Platt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-10"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup> Enju is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Daisuke_Ono" title="Daisuke Ono">Daisuke Ono</a> and English dubbed by <a href="/wiki/Jason_C._Miller" title="Jason C. Miller">Jason C. Miller</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff_2-11"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_staff-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_dub-3">[2]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_work">Original work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Original work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rozen_Maiden_volumes" title="List of Rozen Maiden volumes">List of Rozen Maiden volumes</a></div>
<p><i>Rozen Maiden</i> is authored by <a href="/wiki/Peach-Pit" title="Peach-Pit">Peach-Pit</a> and was serialized in <a href="/wiki/Gentosha" title="Gentosha">Gentosha</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monthly_Comic_Birz" title="Monthly Comic Birz">Monthly Comic Birz</a></i> between issues September 2002 and July 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Birz_September_2002_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Birz_September_2002-23">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st_ending_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-1st_ending-24">[9]</a></sup> Gentosha compiled the individual chapters into eight <i><a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankōbon">tankōbon</a></i> volumes released between March 2003 and June 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st_Vol_1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-1st_Vol_1-25">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st_Vol_8_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-1st_Vol_8-26">[11]</a></sup> These volumes were later recompiled into seven <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shins%C5%8Dban" title="Shinsōban">shinsōban</a></i> volumes by <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a> and released between April 2008 and November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st_Shinso_Vol_1_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-1st_Shinso_Vol_1-27">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st_Shinso_Vol_7_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-1st_Shinso_Vol_7-28">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tokyopop" title="Tokyopop">Tokyopop</a> localized Gentosha's <i>tankōbon</i> volumes in English for North America and released them between May 2006 and May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TP_Vol_1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-TP_Vol_1-29">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TP_Vol_8_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-TP_Vol_8-30">[15]</a></sup> In 2011, Tokyopop's North American division was closed down and their licenses to manga franchises were revoked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tokyopop_Shutdown_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tokyopop_Shutdown-31">[16]</a></sup> Tokyopop's translations were distributed in Australasia by <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">Madman Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[17]</a></sup> The series has also been localized in other languages such as Chinese, French, and Italian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese-33">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-French-34">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italian_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italian-35">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2008, Peach-Pit published a <a href="/wiki/One-shot_(comics)" title="One-shot (comics)">one-shot</a> titled <i>Shōjo no Tsukurikata</i> <span style="font-weight:normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">少女のつくり方</span><span class="t_nihongo_help"><sup><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span style="color:#00e; font:bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration:none; padding:0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup></span>, lit. "How to Make a Girl")</span> in the 16th issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Young_Jump" title="Weekly Young Jump">Weekly Young Jump</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HtMaG_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-HtMaG-36">[21]</a></sup> In the following issue, a serialization for <i>Rozen Maiden</i> was announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Second_Serialization_ANN_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Second_Serialization_ANN-37">[22]</a></sup> Serialization began in <i>Weekly Young Jump</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 20th issue in April 2008 until its conclusion in the issue 8 in January 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Second_Serialization_ANN_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Second_Serialization_ANN-37">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Final_Chapter_Release_Date_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Final_Chapter_Release_Date-38">[23]</a></sup> The second series was published under the <a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">katakana</a> for <i>Rozen Maiden</i><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_KK"><a href="#endnote_KK">KK</a></sup>, and is a sequel to the first series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Title_difference_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Title_difference-39">[24]</a></sup> The series has been localized in other languages such as Italian, French, and Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italian_2_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italian_2-40">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_2_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-French_2-41">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese_2_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese_2-42">[27]</a></sup> Peach-Pit also published a one-shot in the October 2013 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Ribon" title="Ribon">Ribon</a></i> which focuses on the Rozen Maidens' past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_2013_oneshot_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-October_2013_oneshot-43">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_adaptations">Media adaptations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Media adaptations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">Anime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Anime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rozen_Maiden_episodes" title="List of Rozen Maiden episodes">List of Rozen Maiden episodes</a></div>
<p><i>Rozen Maiden</i> was adapted into an anime, produced by <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">Tokyo Broadcasting System</a> and animated by <a href="/wiki/Nomad_(company)" title="Nomad (company)">Nomad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_1_staff_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_1_staff-44">[29]</a></sup> It premiered on Tokyo Broadcasting System and was broadcast between October 7, 2004 and December 23, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBS_premier_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-TBS_premier-45">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_1_episodes_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_1_episodes-46">[31]</a></sup> It was also broadcast on <a href="/wiki/RKB_Mainichi_Broadcasting" title="RKB Mainichi Broadcasting">RKB Mainichi Broadcasting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainichi_Broadcasting_System" title="Mainichi Broadcasting System">Mainichi Broadcasting System</a>, <a href="/wiki/BS-TBS" title="BS-TBS">BS-i</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kids_Station" title="Kids Station">Kids Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broadcast_1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broadcast_1-47">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kids_Station_1_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kids_Station_1-48">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pony_Canyon" title="Pony Canyon">Pony Canyon</a> released the series in six DVDs and a box set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DVDs_anime1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-DVDs_anime1-49">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_1_box_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_1_box-50">[35]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneon_Universal_Entertainment" title="Geneon Universal Entertainment">Geneon USA</a> localized the series for North America and released it on three DVD volumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NA_licenses_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-NA_licenses-51">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_DVD_1_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_DVD_1-52">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_DVD_1_LE_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_DVD_1_LE-53">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_DVD_2_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_DVD_2-54">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_DVD_3_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_DVD_3-55">[40]</a></sup> In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">Funimation</a> gained distribution rights from Geneon and released a box collection of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_DVD_Box_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_DVD_Box-56">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sentai_Filmworks" title="Sentai Filmworks">Sentai Filmworks</a> licensed the series in 2011 and included it in the Rozen Maiden: The Complete Collection DVD box release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NA_licenses_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-NA_licenses-51">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Complete_Collection_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Complete_Collection-57">[42]</a></sup> Sentai also made the series available for streaming on networks such as <a href="/wiki/Anime_Network" title="Anime Network">Anime Network</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crunchyroll" title="Crunchyroll">Crunchyroll</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_Stream_anime1_1_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_Stream_anime1_1-58">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eng_Stream_anime1_12_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eng_Stream_anime1_12-59">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crunchyroll_streaming_1.262_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crunchyroll_streaming_1.262-60">[45]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MVM_Films" title="MVM Films">MVM Films</a> distributed the series in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKV_DVD_1_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-MKV_DVD_1-61">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second series, <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ローゼンメイデン トロイメント</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rōzen Meiden Toroimento</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, was first announced in March 2005 and is a continuation of the previous series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_announced_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_announced-62">[47]</a></sup> It premiered on Tokyo Broadcasting System and was broadcast between October 20, 2005 and January 26, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_episodes_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_episodes-63">[48]</a></sup> It was also broadcast on Mainichi Broadcasting System, <a href="/wiki/Chubu-Nippon_Broadcasting" title="Chubu-Nippon Broadcasting">Chubu-Nippon Broadcasting</a>, BS-i, and Kids Station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_broadcast_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_broadcast-64">[49]</a></sup> Pony Canyon released the series in six DVDs and a box set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_DVDs_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_DVDs-65">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_box_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_box-66">[51]</a></sup> As for the first series, Geneon USA localized the series for North America and released the first volume before closing all DVD distribution in September 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_license_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_license-67">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geneon_DVD_closure_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geneon_DVD_closure-68">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geneon_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geneon_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_1-69">[54]</a></sup> Following Funimation acquiring the distribution rights, Funimation released the series in three DVD volumes and later, released a box set for the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_1_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_1-70">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_2-71">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_3_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_DVD_3-72">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_Box_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation_Tr.C3.A4umend_Box-73">[58]</a></sup> Funimation later released a box set which included the first series and <i>Träumend</i> on May 4, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Funimation_1.262_Box_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Funimation_1.262_Box-74">[59]</a></sup> Sentai Filmworks later licensed the series in 2011 and included it in the Rozen Maiden: The Complete Collection DVD box release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NA_licenses_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-NA_licenses-51">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Complete_Collection_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Complete_Collection-57">[42]</a></sup> Sentai made the series available for streaming on networks such as Anime Network and Crunchyroll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crunchyroll_streaming_1.262_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crunchyroll_streaming_1.262-60">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN_April_2012_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-AN_April_2012-75">[60]</a></sup> MVM Films distributed the series in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MKV_DVD_1bf_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-MKV_DVD_1bf-76">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The third series is <i>Rozen Maiden: Ouvertüre</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ローゼンメイデン オーベルテューレ</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Rōzen Meiden Ōberutyūre</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, a two episode series which explores Suigintou's origins. It premiered on Tokyo Broadcasting System and was broadcast on December 22 and 23, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ouvert.C3.BCre_episodes_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ouvert.C3.BCre_episodes-77">[62]</a></sup> The episodes were released on DVD on February 21, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ouvert.C3.BCre_DVD_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ouvert.C3.BCre_DVD-78">[63]</a></sup> Sentai Filmworks licensed the series in 2011 and included it in the Rozen Maiden: The Complete Collection DVD box release and as a stand-alone DVD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NA_licenses_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-NA_licenses-51">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Complete_Collection_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Complete_Collection-57">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Ouvert.C3.BCre_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Ouvert.C3.BCre-79">[64]</a></sup> Sentai made the series available for streaming on Anime Network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AN_June_2012_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-AN_June_2012-80">[65]</a></sup> MVM Films distributed the series in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MVM_ODVD_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-MVM_ODVD-81">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fourth series is <i>Rozen Maiden: Zurückspulen</i>, referred only as <i>Rozen Maiden</i><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_KK"><a href="#endnote_KK">KK</a></sup> in Japan, was announced in November 2012 in <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Young_Jump" title="Weekly Young Jump">Weekly Young Jump</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WYJ_52_2012_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-WYJ_52_2012-82">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_ANN_announce_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_ANN_announce-83">[68]</a></sup> It is an adaption of the second manga series. Unlike the previous three anime series, it is animated by <a href="/wiki/Studio_Deen" title="Studio Deen">Studio Deen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_staff-5">[3]</a></sup> It premiered on Tokyo Broadcasting System and was broadcast between July 4, 2013 and September 26, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_episodes_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_episodes-84">[69]</a></sup> It was also broadcast on Mainichi Broadcasting System, Chubu-Nippon Broadcasting, and <a href="/wiki/BS-TBS" title="BS-TBS">BS-TBS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_broadcast_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_broadcast-85">[70]</a></sup> Crunchyroll licensed the series for <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">simulcast</a> followed by Sentai Filmworks who made it available for simulcast on Anime Network and released the series on home video in October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_simulcast_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_simulcast-86">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_announce_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_announce-87">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Network_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Network_Zur.C3.BCckspulen-88">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sentai_Zuruck_release_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sentai_Zuruck_release-89">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rozen_Maiden_discography" title="Rozen Maiden discography">Rozen Maiden discography</a></div>
<p>The four anime series resulted in several <a href="/wiki/Theme_music" title="Theme music">theme music</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_drama_in_Japan" title="Radio drama in Japan">radio dramas</a>, soundtracks, and two <a href="/wiki/Radio_program" title="Radio program">radio programs</a>. The first radio program is <i>Rozen Maiden Web Radio: Rose Scented Garden Party</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[Jp 16]</a></sup>, an <a href="/wiki/Internet_radio" title="Internet radio">internet radio</a> program that aired on <a href="/wiki/Lantis_(company)" title="Lantis (company)">Lantis Web Radio</a> between May 13, 2005 and September 30, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSGP_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSGP-91">[75]</a></sup> It is hosted by Miyuki Sawashiro and Asami Sanada, the voice of Shinku and Jun respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSGP_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSGP-91">[75]</a></sup> The second is <i>Suigintou's Night of Ennui</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[Jp 17]</a></sup>, a <a href="/wiki/Live_radio" title="Live radio">live radio</a> hosted by Sugintou's voice actress Rie Tanaka during Tokyo Broadcasting System's Anime Festa 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Night_of_Ennui_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Night_of_Ennui-93">[76]</a></sup> Due to positive reception, it was continued through additional CD releases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Night_of_Ennui_adaption_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Night_of_Ennui_adaption-94">[77]</a></sup> The soundtracks from the <i>Rozen Maiden</i> video games have also been released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beilege_1_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beilege_1-95">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beilege_2_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beilege_2-96">[79]</a></sup> Prior to the anime's creation, a radio drama was produced by <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Works" title="Frontier Works">Frontier Works</a> who used their own voice cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CD_drama_1_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-CD_drama_1-97">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CD_drama_1_voice_cast_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-CD_drama_1_voice_cast-98">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Three video games have been produced for the series. <i>Rozen Maiden: Duellwalzer</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[Jp 18]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> video game developed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taito_Corporation" title="Taito Corporation">Taito Corporation</a> and released on April 27, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duellwalzer_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duellwalzer-100">[82]</a></sup> Its soundtrack, <i>Rozen Maiden Beilege Disk</i>, was included with the game's preorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beilege_1_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beilege_1-95">[78]</a></sup> The game re-released under the label "Taito Best" on March 25, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duellwalzer_TB_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duellwalzer_TB-101">[83]</a></sup> Taito released a second game for the PlayStation 2 titled <i>Rozen Maiden: Gebetgarten</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[Jp 19]</a></sup> on March 22, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gebetgarten_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gebetgarten-103">[84]</a></sup> Its soundtrack, <i>Rozen Maiden Beilege Disk 2</i>, was included with the preorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beilege_2_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beilege_2-96">[79]</a></sup> The third video game is <i>Rozen Maiden: Wechseln Sie Welt Ab</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[Jp 20]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/5pb." title="5pb.">5pb.</a> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Vita" title="PlayStation Vita">PlayStation Vita</a>; it was released on January 30, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wechseln_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wechseln-105">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anthology_manga_and_novels">Anthology manga and novels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Anthology manga and novels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several manga <a href="/wiki/Spin-off_(media)" title="Spin-off (media)">spin-offs</a> were created. An anthology <i>tankōbon</i> entitled <i>Rozen Maiden: Entr'acte</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[Jp 21]</a></sup> was published by Getonsha in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Entracte_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Entracte-107">[86]</a></sup> Two anthology series were created based on the second series. The first is <i>Rozen Maiden Dolls Talk</i><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_KK"><a href="#endnote_KK">KK</a></sup> by Haru Karuki. It was serialized in <i><a href="/wiki/Ribon" title="Ribon">Ribon</a></i> between the January 2012 to April 2014 issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribon_January_2012_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ribon_January_2012-108">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dolls_Talk_end_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dolls_Talk_end-109">[88]</a></sup> The second is <i>Maite wa Ikenai Rozen Maiden</i> <span style="font-weight:normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">まいてはいけないローゼンメイデン</span><span class="t_nihongo_help"><sup><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span style="color:#00e; font:bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration:none; padding:0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup></span>, lit. "The Rozen Maiden That Should Not Have Existed")</span> by Choboraunyopomi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maite_wa_Serialization_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maite_wa_Serialization-110">[89]</a></sup> It began serialization in <i>Miracle Jump</i> issue 12, which was released on December 27, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maite_wa_Serialization_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maite_wa_Serialization-110">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miracle_Jump_12_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miracle_Jump_12-111">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two anthology novel series have been written. Chabō Higurashi wrote the anthology novel series <i>Die Romane der Rozen Maiden</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[Jp 22]</a></sup> which consisted of two novels subtitled <i>Schwarzer Wind</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[Jp 23]</a></sup> and <i>Kalkgrün Augen</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schwarzer_Wind_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schwarzer_Wind-114">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalkgr.C3.BCn_Augen_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalkgr.C3.BCn_Augen-115">[92]</a></sup> Himiro Hisasa wrote the second novel series, <i>Rozen Maiden</i><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_KK"><a href="#endnote_KK">KK</a></sup>, which consisted of two novels subtitled <i>Zwillinge</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[Jp 24]</a></sup> and <i>Roth Schwarz</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[Jp 25]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zwillinge_novel_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zwillinge_novel-118">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roth_Schwarz_novel_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roth_Schwarz_novel-119">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Rozen Maiden</i> anime has been adapted into three <a href="/wiki/Film_comic" title="Film comic">film comic</a> volumes by <a href="/wiki/Gentosha" title="Gentosha">Gentosha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_Comic_1_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Film_Comic_1-120">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_Comic_2_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Film_Comic_2-121">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_Comic_3_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Film_Comic_3-122">[97]</a></sup> Two fan books based on the anime were also published: <i>Rozen Maiden: Edel Rose</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[Jp 26]</a></sup> covers the anime <i>Rozen Maiden</i> and is published by Impress Group;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edel_Rose_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edel_Rose-124">[98]</a></sup> <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend Nocturne</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[Jp 27]</a></sup> covers <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> and is published by Gentosha;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_Nocturne_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_Nocturne-126">[99]</a></sup> <i>Rozen Maiden Comic &amp; Anime Official Guide Book</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[Jp 28]</a></sup> covers <i>Rozen Maiden: Zurückspulen</i> and is published by Shueisha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fan_book_3_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fan_book_3-128">[100]</a></sup> Four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_book" title="Art book">art books</a> were also released: <i>Rozen Maiden: Erinnerung</i> published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SoftBank_Creative" title="SoftBank Creative">SoftBank Creative</a>, <i>Rozen Maiden: Kunstwerk</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[Jp 29]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Ichijinsha" title="Ichijinsha">Ichijinsha</a>, <i>Peach-Pit Art book (Rozen Maiden)</i> and <i>Rozen Maiden Art Book: Rose Maiden</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[Jp 30]</a></sup>, both by <a href="/wiki/Shueisha" title="Shueisha">Shueisha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erinnerung_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Erinnerung-131">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunstwerk_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kunstwerk-132">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peach-Pit_Art_book_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peach-Pit_Art_book-133">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_Maiden_art_book_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rose_Maiden_art_book-134">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many merchandise has been released based on the <i>Rozen Maiden</i> franchise such as dolls, clothing and accessories, and other miscellaneous items.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rozen_Maiden_goods_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rozen_Maiden_goods-135">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tr.C3.A4umend_goods_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tr.C3.A4umend_goods-136">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ouvert.C3.BCre_goods_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ouvert.C3.BCre_goods-137">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_goods_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zur.C3.BCckspulen_goods-138">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Movic_goods_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Movic_goods-139">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tokyopop" title="Tokyopop">Tokyopop</a>'s localized volumes appeared on ICv2's monthly top one-hundred selling graphic novels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICv2_Vol1_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICv2_Vol1-140">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICv2_Vol3_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICv2_Vol3-141">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICv2_Vol4_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICv2_Vol4-142">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICv2_Vol5_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICv2_Vol5-143">[113]</a></sup> The <i>Rozen Maiden</i> manga has received generally positive reviews. <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">Anime News Network</a> praised Peach-Pit's works as always being able to evoke excitement or laughter from its readers but was critical about <i>Rozen Maiden</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s lack of plot and criticized how the dialogue or layout can be vague.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Manga_4_review_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Manga_4_review-144">[114]</a></sup> Comic Book Bin wrote that while <i>Rozen Maiden</i> was not a splendid manga, its emphasis on psychology and emotion was something American comics should follow to expand their readership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBB_review_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBB_review-145">[115]</a></sup> Active Anime praised several aspects of the series: the combination of mystery, comedy, and cuteness with a balance of fantasy and drama;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_Manga_2_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_Manga_2-146">[116]</a></sup> the visual esthetics of the images and characters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_Manga_6_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_Manga_6-147">[117]</a></sup> and a broadness that extends towards teens and adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_Manga_3_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_Manga_3-148">[118]</a></sup> Initially, Anime Land praised the balance between comedic daily life and the underlying dark side of the plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga_2_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga_2-149">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga_3_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga_3-150">[120]</a></sup> In later volumes though, Anime Land criticized the story's pacing and the abrupt ending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga_5_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga_5-151">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga_6_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga_6-152">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga_7_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga_7-153">[123]</a></sup> In their review of the sequel, Anime Land wrote they were surprised by the dark tone and how the plot was confusing even with knowledge from the first series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga2_1_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga2_1-154">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anime_Land_manga2_2_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anime_Land_manga2_2-155">[125]</a></sup> Manga-News also praised the story's alteration between moments of peace and conflict but panned the latter volumes for being rushed and losing the story's complexity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manga_News_series_review_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manga_News_series_review-156">[126]</a></sup> In their review of the sequel, Manga-News praised the introduction for being interesting and accessible to new readers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manga-News_S2_1_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manga-News_S2_1-157">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Japanese television network <a href="/wiki/TV_Asahi" title="TV Asahi">TV Asahi</a> conducted a "Top 100" online web poll and the <i>Rozen Maiden</i> anime adaptation placed 50th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[128]</a></sup> In the subsequent year, <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> ranked 7th in a "Top 20" poll conducted by Japanese anime magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">Animage</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[129]</a></sup> Active Anime had several reviewers for the anime series <i>Rozen Maiden</i> and its sequel <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i>. Christopher Seaman wrote several praises for the anime: the high quality visuals and the detail in the dolls' designs; the soundtrack which compliments the visuals; and the story which he considered to be engaging, fast paced, and comedic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_DVD_1_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_DVD_1-160">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_DVD_3_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_DVD_3-161">[131]</a></sup> Sandra Scholes described the series as a lavish production and that while it is battle oriented during fight scenes, it also offers emotional moments that cater to girls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_DVD_2_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_DVD_2-162">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_TDVD_1_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_TDVD_1-163">[133]</a></sup> Davey C. Jones commented the series is something <i><a href="/wiki/Chobits" title="Chobits">Chobits</a></i> fans would enjoy and that <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s ending is not a "feel good" ending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_TCollection_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_TCollection-164">[134]</a></sup> Rachel Bentham however, was critical of the plot. Bentham described Jun's antisocial personality and friendship with the dolls to be disturbing and criticized the "there can be only one" competition between the dolls calling it misogynistic in nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA_Complete_Collection_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA_Complete_Collection-165">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mania initially expressed skepticism of the show's combination of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gothic_lolita" title="Gothic lolita">gothic lolita</a>, dolls, magic, and comedy but later calls it a successful experiment and praised the character interactions and the dolls' designs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mania_DVD_1_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mania_DVD_1-166">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mania_DVD_2_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mania_DVD_2-167">[137]</a></sup> In their <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> review, Mania praised the visuals and characters but criticized the unbalanced comic and dark comments and described the revelations and finale as rushed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mania_TDVD_2_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mania_TDVD_2-168">[138]</a></sup> Anime News Network's review of <i>Rozen Maiden: Träumend</i> were mostly negative and addressed several points: the failed attempts at serious drama which were considered cliché and resulted in cheesy and melodramatic dialogue;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Traumend_1_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Traumend_1-169">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Traumend_2_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Traumend_2-170">[140]</a></sup> the recycled background music; and the ending which was described as inconclusive and slapdash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Traumend_3_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Traumend_3-171">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anime News Network's reviews of <i>Rozen Maiden: Zurückspulen</i> was generally positive. Carl Kimlinger described the characterization of the adult Jun as a "highly believable mixture of bruised pride, desperate loneliness, and downtrodden numbness" and praised how relatable the character is compared to his younger self.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_1_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_1-172">[142]</a></sup> He also praised the scripting for Jun's life and the scene where Jun's personality is being dissected by his boss to be intelligently written. Bamboo Dong praised <i>Zurückspulen</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s introduction for revitalizing the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_2_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_2-173">[143]</a></sup> Both reviewers praised the art and dolls' designs and expressed concerns about the confusing plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_1_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_1-172">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_2_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_Zur.C3.BCckspulen_2-173">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rozen_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Phase"><b><a href="#ref_Phase">^</a></b></span> Prologue 1 &amp; 2 are the first two chapters from the <i>Rozen Maiden</i> manga. Afterwards, chapters are referred to as Phases starting with Phase 1.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Tale"><b><a href="#ref_Tale">^</a></b></span> Tales are what chapters from the sequel manga series are referred as. The sequel is published under the katakana for <i>Rozen Maiden</i>.</li>
<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_KK"><b><a href="#ref_KK">^</a></b></span> The <a href="/wiki/Katakana" title="Katakana">katakana</a> for <i>Rozen Maiden</i> is <span class="t_nihongo_kanji"><span lang="ja">ローゼンメイデン</span></span>. KK denotes <i>Rozen Maiden</i> as being written in katakana instead of the English alphabet.</li>
</ul>
</div>
